## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic constitutive laws and temperature modifies material stiffness and strength through thermal softening mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent linear elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (modulus decreasing linearly with T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (rational): sigma = c0 * epsilon * c1 / (c2 + T) (thermal softening of elastic modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear strain hardening)
- Temperature-dependent power-law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T)**c3 (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic strain hardening)
- Johnson-Cook type (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Arrhenius thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * c2 / T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (exponential decrease of strength with T)
- Neo-Hookean rubber elasticity: sigma = c0 * (c1 - c2 * T) * (epsilon - c3 * epsilon**(-2)) (hyperelastic with thermal dependence)
- Voce-type saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating stress with thermal softening)
- Polynomial constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial stress-strain curve)
- Thermal expansion offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress accounting for thermal strain)
- Combined model: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T)**c2 * exp(-c3 * T) (thermal strain offset with exponential softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear thermal softening (modulus decreasing with T) → multiplicative factor (c0 - c1*T) or (1 - c0*T**c1)
- Thermal strain offset → stress depends on (epsilon - c*T) rather than epsilon alone, reflecting thermal expansion
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicates stress approaching a plateau at large strains
- Thermally activated processes → exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) terms capturing Arrhenius-type temperature dependence
- Elastic-plastic transition → sum of linear term (c0*epsilon) and nonlinear term (c1*epsilon**c2) representing distinct deformation regimes
- Homologous temperature scaling → T appears as ratio c0*T or (T - c1)/(c2 - c1) normalizing to melting point
- Strain-temperature coupling asymmetry → at low T stress is more sensitive to strain; at high T stress is more sensitive to T, suggesting product forms with different exponents
- Concavity change in stress-strain → cubic or higher-order polynomial terms, or rational functions, indicating inflection points in hardening behavior
